рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

тАШрдордзреНрд╡рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреГрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдФрд╢рд┐рдЬрд╕реНрдп рдХрдХреНрд╖реАрд╡рдд рдЖрд░реНрд╖рдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдорд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирдореН ред тАШрдордзреНрд╡рдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН рее рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗрди рд╕рд╣реЛрдХреНрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

+Jamison Brereton

117
As╠Бvins
Kakс╣г─лvant Dairghatamasa
25 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This hymn is a catalogue of the heroic deeds of the A┼Ыvins, which ultimately leads to the poetтАЩs request for heroes (vs. 25). The problem for the poet is that such a hymn listing so many of the godsтАЩ deeds could easily become just an inventory without any real coherence. One of the poetтАЩs solutions to this problem is to create verbal and thematic linkages among verses and sets of verses in order to organize and unify his composition.
At the highest level the great deeds of the A┼Ыvins are arranged according to theme. First are deeds in which the A┼Ыvins rescue those who have been hidden away in some fashion: Atri in the earth cleft (3), Rebha in the waters (4), and Vandana in the ground (5). Then, the poet shifts from the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ rescues to their generosity. The theme is announced in verse 6 and then exemplified in verses 7тАУ9. The A┼Ыvins give the gift of a wife (7ab) and husband (7cd), a bright body (8ab), fame (8cd), and a horse (9). Verse 10 then summarizes this theme and announces a new one

that extends the image of the horse in verse 9. The deeds in the next section turn on the A┼Ыvins as charioteers and horsemen. They bring prizes to the poet (11ab) and restore the racing mare Vi┼Ыpal─Б (11d). Verses 12тАУ16 connect the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ deeds to the journeys of their chariot and horses. On those journeys they come to the aid of Cyav─Бna, Bhujyu, and others. The last extended set of verses, verses 16тАУ22, describe a variety of different acts, but all these verses mention animals: a quail (16), sheep and a she-wolf (17тАУ18), a barren cow (20), a тАЬwolfтАЭ (possibly a plow; 21), and the head of a horse (22). This leaves aside verse 19, but the тАЬlame oneтАЭ here is probably the mare Vi┼Ыpal─Б, one suggestion of S─Бyaс╣Зa. Note that the last two sets of verses overlap at verse 16, a join that again helps hold the poem together.
Another way the poet creates a sense of unity is by the repetition of lexical items, sometimes used in different contexts. So, the poet uses the unusual verb sa╠Бm тИЪr─л тАЬdraw back togetherтАЭ in verses 4, 11, and 19 to describe a rescue from the sea, the repair of a horse, and the healing of the тАЬlame one.тАЭ Or again, the A┼Ыvins carried down (n├н…┼лhathuс╕е) a horse or a bride (9b, 20d) and carried Bhujyu out (n├нс╕е…┼лhathuс╕е) of the sea (14d, 15c). In 5c n├нkh─Бta тАЬburiedтАЭ describes Vandana; n├нkh─Бta occurs again in 12c, although it is not clear to whom the latter verse refers. S─Бyaс╣Зa suggests that it is Rebha, who was тАЬburiedтАЭ in the waters, an interpretation supported by the reference to the tenth day (cf. I.116.24). However, since the verb n├нkh─Бta was just used with Vandana in verse 5cd, it may be he to whom the verse refers.
Likewise, the poet links consecutive verses by repeating the same or similar words. The A┼Ыvins rescue the seer (┼Х╠ес╣гi) Atri in 3a and the seer Rebha in 4b. Each of verses 20тАУ22 addresses the a┼Ыvin─Б and the тАЬwondrous onesтАЭ (dasr─Б/dasrau). The four hemistichs of verses 13 and 14 all begin with yuvo╠Бс╕е or yuva╠Бm. Verses 15 and 16 both begin a╠Бjohav─лt тАЬhe called again and again.тАЭ Such verbal concatenation again helps unify the diverse contents of the hymn.
The poet explores other kinds of verbal play, some of which create intercon nections within the poem, but others reflect other purposes or simply his artistry as a poet. For example, v├нс╣гakta тАЬdroopingтАЭ of 20a is phonologically rearranged in 24c as the rare word v├нkasta тАЬsplit apart.тАЭ There appears to be another phonologi cal connection in verse 16cd between viс╣гv─Б╠Бc, the personal name Viс╣гv─Бc, which may mean the тАЬDouble-Talker,тАЭ and viс╣гa╠Б тАЬpoison.тАЭ However, the interpretation of this hemistich is problematic, in part because Viс╣гv─Бc and his son are only attested here. Geldner and others understand the poison to be the means by which the A┼Ыvins destroy the son of Viс╣гv─Бc, but if so, such use of poison by the A┼Ыvins is isolated. Rather, the poison may have given rise to the son of Viс╣гv─Бc, an interpretation sup ported by the phonological similarity of viс╣гv─Б╠Бc and viс╣гa╠Б. Perhaps the idea is that Viс╣гv─БcтАЩs son is born from the тАЬpoisonтАЭ of his тАЬdouble-talkingтАЭ speech.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins for your gratification by the plural asant Soma, your ancient worshipper adores you; the offering is poured upon the sacred gras, thehymn is ready (for repetition); come, N─Бsatyas, with food and with vigour.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The age-old Hotar [=Agni] seeks to win you in order for you to be exhilarated on the honeyed soma, o A┼Ыvins.
The gift accompanied by the ritual grass is laid out, (as is) my song. With refreshment, with prizes of victory, journey here, o N─Бsatyas.

+Griffith

ASVINS, your ancient priest invites you hither to gladden you with draughts of meath of Soma.
Our gift is on the grass, our song apportioned: with food and strength come hither, O Nasatyas.

+Geldner

Zum Rausche des s├╝├Яen Soma bittet euch, Asvin, der alte Hotri her. F├╝r die Darbringung ist das Barhis hergerichtet, die Rede ist verteilt. Kommet herbei mit Labsal, mit Belohnungen, ihr Nasatya┬┤s!

+Grassmann

Zum Trunk des s├╝ssen Soma’s euch zum Rausche, o Ritter, lockt euch her der alte Priester, Die Gab’ ist aufgestellt, das Lied erklungen, o Treue, kommet her mit Trank und Speise.

тАЬWith that car, A┼Ыvins, which, rapid as thought, drawn by good horses, appears before men, and withwhich you repair to the dwelling of the virtuous, come, leaders of (sacrifice), to our abode.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Your chariot, o A┼Ыvins, swifter than mind, drawn by good horses, comes to the clans.
By which (chariot) you go to the home of the good ritual performer, by that, o men, travel your course to us.

+Griffith

That car of yours, swifter than thought, O Asvins, which drawn by brave steeds cometh to the people,
Whereon ye seek the dwelling of the pious,–come ye thereon to our abode, O Heroes.

+Geldner

Euer Wagen, ihr Asvin, der schneller als der Gedanke, mit guten Rossen bespannt. Die Clane besucht, mit dem ihr zum Hause des Frommen kommet, auf den machet die Umfahrt zu uns, ihr Herren!

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou liberated, leaders (of rites), the sage Atri, who was venerated by the five classes of men from the wicked prison, together with his troop (of children), destroying his enemies and baffling, showerers (of benefits), the devices of the malignant Dasyus.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You free Atri, the seer of the five peoples, from narrow straits, from the earth cleft along with his band, o menтАФ
confounding the wiles of the merciless Dasyu, driving them out, one after another, o bulls.

+Griffith

Ye freed sage Atri, whom the Five Tribes honoured, from the strait pit, ye Heroes with his people,
Baffling the guiles of the malignant Dasyu, repelling them, ye Mighty in succession.

+Geldner

Den unter den f├╝nf St├дmmen bekannten Rishi Atri befreit ihr Herren aus Drangsal, mit seinem Gefolge aus dem gl├╝henden Ofen, indem ihr die Listen des feindseligen Dasyu vereitelt habt, einen nach dem anderen zur Eile treibend, ihr Bullen.

+Grassmann

Den Seher Atri der f├╝nf St├дmme l├╢stet sammt seiner Schar aus enger Kluft ihr Helden, Des unheilvollen D├дmons Zauber tilgend, und jenen vorw├дrtstreibend, o ihr Stiere.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThat (exploit) of yours, leaders (of sacrifice), is to be celebrated, N─Бsatyas, by Kakс╣г─лvat, of the race of Pajra, when you filled for the (expectant) man a hundred vases of sweet (liquors) from the hoof of your fleet horse.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

This (deed) of yours in your earth-encircling course, o men, deserves to be praised by Kakс╣г─лvant, the son of Pajra, o N─Бsatyas:
from the hoof of your prizewinning horse, you poured a hundred pots of honey for the people.

+Griffith

Kaksivan, Pajra’s son, must laud that exploit of yours, Nasatyas, Heroes, ye who wander!
When from the hoof of your strong horse ye showered a hundred jars of honey for the people.

+Geldner

+Grassmann

Dies Werk, o treue M├дnner, ist zu r├╝hmen vom Padschrasohn Kakschivat aller Orten; Dass aus des schnellen Rosses Huf den Menschen ihr hundert K├╝bel s├╝ssen Tranks ergosset.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou restored, leaders (of sacrifices), Viс╣гс╣З─Бpu (his lost son) to Vi┼Ыvaka, the son of Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa, when he praised you; you bestowed, A┼Ыvins, a husband upon Ghoс╣г─Б, growing old and tarrying inher father’s dwelling.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ghoс╣г─Б was the daughter of Kakс╣г─лvat; she was a leper, and therefore, unfit to be married; but when advanced in years, she prayed to the A┼Ыvins, who healed her leprosy and restored her to youth and beauty, so that she obtained a husband

+Jamison Brereton

You two, o men, gave Viс╣гс╣З─Бp┼л to Vi┼Ыvaka Kr╠ес╣гс╣Зiya, who was
praising you.
Even to Ghoс╣г─Б, living at home with her father, you gave a husband, though she was growing old, A┼Ыvins.

+Griffith

To Krsna’s son, to Visvaka who praised you, O Heroes, ye restored his son Visnapu.
To Ghosa, living in her father’s dwelling, stricken in years, ye gave a husband, Asvins.

+Geldner

Ihr Herren gabt dem lobpreisenden Visvaka Krisniya den Visnapu wieder. Auch der Ghosa, die zu Hause bei den Eltern sitzen geblieben, gabet ihr Asvin noch im Alter einen Gemahl.

+Grassmann

Dem Vi├зvaka, dem Krischnaspross, o M├дnner, dem S├дnger habt Vischnapu ihr gegeben; Der Ghoscha auch, die in des Vaters Hauss sass, gabt, als sie alt war, Ritter, ihr den Gatten.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins, who assume many forms, you gave to Pedu a swift horse, the bringer of a thousand (treasures), powerful, irresistible, the destroyer of foes, the object of praise, the bearer (over dangers).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Assuming many forms, A┼Ыvins, you carried down a swift horse to Pedu, an unstoppable prizewinning horse that gains a thousand (cows), a
smasher of serpents, deserving to be famed as the surpassing one.

+Griffith

O Asvins, wearing many forms at pleasure, on Pedu ye bestowed a fleet-foot courser,
Strong, winner of a thousand spoils, resistless the serpent slayer, glorious, triumphant.

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬDissipators of affliction, as you were praised with former praises by Tugra, so were you again adored (by him), when you brought Bhujyu safe from the tossing ocean with swift ships and rapid horses.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vibhiс╕е = swift naubhiс╕е (ships)

+Jamison Brereton

You turned your minds again to Tugra in your ancient ways, o youthful ones.
You carried Bhujyu from the flood, from the sea, with your birds, your silvery horses.

+Griffith

Ye, ever-youthful Ones, again remembered Tugra, according to your ancient manner:
With horses brown of hue that flew with swift wings ye brought back Bhujyu from the sea of billows.

+Geldner

Ihr J├╝nglinge waret dem Tugra mit dem fr├╝heren Eifer wieder zugeneigt. Ihr holtet den Bhujyu aus der Meeresflut heraus mit den V├╢geln, den Schimmelrossen.

+Grassmann

An Tugra habt nach euren alten Weisen, o ewig junge, ihr euch neu erinnert, Ihr fuhrt den Bhudschju aus des Meeres Wogen heraus mit euren rothen Fl├╝gelrossen.

+Elizarenkova

тАЬTh sun of Tugra, brought back by you, A┼Ыvins, (to his father), glorified you whenhe ahd crossed the ocean in safety, and you bore him, showerers (of benefits), with your well-harnessed car, swift as thought, to safety.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Carried forth into the sea, the son of Tugra [=Bhujyu] called upon you again and again, having gone (to you) on an unwavering course, A┼Ыvins. You carried him out with your chariot, swift as mind, with its good team, o bulls, to keep him well.

+Griffith

The son of Tugra had invoked you, Asvins; borne on he went uninjured through the ocean.
Ye with your chariot swift as thought, well-harnessed, carried him off, O Mighty Ones, to safety.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe quail glorified you, A┼Ыvins, when you saved her from the mouth of the wolf; you carried off (J─Бhuс╣гa) to the top of the mountain in your triumphant chariot; and slew the son of Viс╣гv─Б├▒c with a poisoned (arrow).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Viс╣гv─Б├▒c is an asura, The text has, ‘whose son you killed with poison’; a poisoned arrow is implied

+Jamison Brereton

The quail-hen called upon you again and again, A┼Ыvins, so that you freed her from the mouth of the wolf.
With your victorious (chariot) you journeyed across the back of the rock. You crushed the (son) of Viс╣гv─Бc [=the Double-Talker?], born by poison.

+Griffith

The quail had invocated you, O Asvins, when from the wolf’s devouring jaws ye freed her.
With conquering car ye cleft the mountain’s ridges: the offspring of Visvac ye killed with poison.

+Geldner

Es hatte euch, Asvin, die Wachtel angerufen, als ihr sie aus dem Rachen des Wolfes befreitet. Mit dem siegreichen Wagen fuhrt ihr durch den R├╝cken des Berges. Die Brut des Visvac habt ihr durch Gift get├╢tet.

+Grassmann

Die Wachtel hatt’, o Ritter, euch gerufen, als ihr sie l├╢stet aus des Wolfes Rachen; Ihr schrittet siegreich durch des Berges R├╝cken und t├╢dtetet mit Gift den Sohn des Vischvak.

To him, Rjrasva, gave ye eyes, O Asvins; light to the blind ye sent for perfect vision.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins, your powerful protection is the source of happiness; worthy of laudation, you have made whole the maimed; therefore, has the intelligent (Ghoс╣г─Б) called upon you; showerers (of benefits) come hither with your succours.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Great is your help, a joy itself, o A┼Ыvins. Even the lame one do you draw back together, o holy ones.
And so Plenty called upon just you two, and you two came to her with your help, o bulls.

+Griffith

Great and weal-giving is your aid, O Asvins, ye, objects of all thought, made whole the cripple.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins, causing the barley to be sown (in the fields that had been prepared) by the plural ugh; milking (the clouds) for the sake of Manu; destroying the Dasyu with the thunderbolt; you have bestowed brilliant light upon the ─Аrya.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

─Аry─Бya: viduс╣гe, to the sage, that is to Manu;

Manuс╣гa = Manu

+Jamison Brereton

O A┼Ыvins, wondrous ones, scattering barley by a тАЬwolfтАЭ [=a drill plow?], milking out refreshment for the race of Manu,
blasting sound at the Dasyu with a bagpipe, you made wide light for the ─Аrya.

+Griffith

Ploughing and sowing barley, O ye Asvins, milking out food for men, ye Wonder-Workers,
Blasting away the Dasyu with your trumpet, ye gave far-spreading light unto the Arya.

Indem ihr mit dem Wolfe Korn s├дtet und dem Menschen Nahrung herausmolket, ihr Meister, und mit dem Bakura den Dasyu anblieset, habt ihr weites Licht f├╝r den Arier bereitet.

+Grassmann

Die Gerste s├дend, Ritter, mit dem Pfluge, und Trank dem Menschen melkend, wunderth├дt’ge! Hinweg Barbaren blasend mit dem Kriegshorn, habt ihr dem Arjer weiten Glanz geschaffen.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou replaced, A┼Ыvins, with the head of a horse, (the head of) Dadhya├▒c, the son of Atharvan, and, true to his promise, he revealed to you the mystic knowledge which he had learned from Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б, and which was as a ligature of the waist to you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б = Indra; the knowlege was kakс╣гyam. v─Бm = a girdle to you both; strengthening them to perform religious rites

+Jamison Brereton

For Dadhya├▒c, the son of Atharvan, you substituted the head of a horse, A┼Ыvins.
Speaking the truth, he proclaimed to you Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs honey, which was hidden from you, o wondrous ones.

+Griffith

Ye brought the horse’s head, Asvins, and gave it unto Dadhyac the offspring of Atharvan.
True, he revealed to you, O Wonder-Workers, sweet Soma, Tvastar’s secret, as your girdle.

+Geldner

Dem Dadhyac, dem Atharvansohn, gabt ihr einen Pferdekopf zum Ersatz. Er verriet euch wahrheitsgetreu die tvastrische S├╝├Яigkeit, die euch verborgen war, ihr Meister.

+Grassmann

Dem Dadhiank, dem Spross Atharvans, habt ihr den Kopf des Pferdes angesetzt, o Ritter, Der redliche hat euch den Meth des Tvaschtar, den, hehre, ihr im Busen bargt, verk├╝ndet.
